British Gunship Lost Cannon 99

Cannon Positioned on Top Deck; Box of Ammunition Also Lost; Investigation Results in Astonishment

Changsha Correspondence – The British warship HMS Aphis, which is anchored off the coast of Changsha, experienced a major theft in the late hours of January 25th. A Lewis gun (transliteration) and a box of Lewis ammunition, both mounted on the ship's deck, were stolen. The details are as follows:

Situation of the British Warship 100

The British warship is named HMS Aphis and is commanded by Captain Cox. It sailed from Hankou to the provincial capital on September 8th of last year and is anchored off the coast. The ship has a total of over sixty British soldiers and employs twenty-four Chinese workers. According to regulations, Chinese workers are not allowed near the gunnery hold and the deck. The lost cannon, called Lewis, was originally mounted in an iron box on the three-story deck. Armed British soldiers were stationed on the deck for surveillance. Nothing unusual was observed on the afternoon of the 25th. On the morning of the 26th, the British soldier on duty discovered that the cannon was missing. At the same time, a box of ammunition was also lost. The incident was reported to the captain, who in turn reported it to the British consul, who then notified the water and land police to investigate.

Investigation and Report 101

After receiving the report, the British consulate immediately dispatched Secretary Xiong Juxian to the Xinguang police station of the Third Water Police Brigade and the Sixth Police Station of the West District of the land-water continent, notifying them to conduct an on-site investigation of the British warship. The investigation was carried out by Wang Baosheng, a patrol officer of the water police station, who prepared a report stating: "According to the report from Xiong Juxian, Secretary of the British Consulate, yesterday (25th) night, the British warship HMS Aphis lost a Lewis gun. I immediately went to the ship with Chen, a patrol officer from the Sixth Police Station of the land-water continent, to investigate the situation. It was reported that the serial number of the lost gun was 544, and a box of Lewis ammunition was also lost, containing ten cakes, each with forty-seven rounds, as well as seventeen rows of .65 caliber bullets. The lost gun was mounted on the ship's deck and guarded by British soldiers. The fact that it was lost is quite astonishing. A detailed report will be submitted in person, and detectives have been ordered to investigate. This report is hereby submitted." At the same time, British Consul Arche sent a letter to the Hunan Provincial Government stating: "Sir, I am writing to inform you that according to a report from Captain Cox of the British warship HMS Aphis, a Lewis gun and a box of Lewis ammunition, containing ten cakes of bullets, each with forty-seven bullets, totaling 470 bullets, and seventeen rows of .65 caliber bullets, were stolen from the ship last night. I have requested the Sixth Police Station of the land-water continent and the Third Water Police Brigade to dispatch patrol officers to conduct an on-site investigation. I am writing to inform your provincial government to investigate, issue a general order to all units of the land and water military and police to conduct a thorough investigation, arrest the perpetrators, and provide a reply. Consul Arche, January 25th."

Troop Transfer Aground 102

It was discovered that on the afternoon of January 25th at 6:00 PM, the British warship Changjiang, led by Captain Sochoro, sailed from Hankou to replace the HMS Aphis. Unexpectedly, the HMS Aphis lost its cannon that evening, leading to many suspicions. Later, the HMS Aphis handed over the lost cannon case to the British consulate for handling. It weighed anchor and prepared to sail to Hankou at 8:30 AM on the 28th. However, due to the dry winter and low water levels, and being unfamiliar with the waterway, it ran aground in the XinKang River. It cannot be moved until the spring floods arrive. The British warship is truly plagued by troubles. (February 1st)

Special Products from Northern Anhui Shipped Sequentially 103

More Than Ten Counties Have Started; Special Products Inspection Station Established in Bengbu

Bengbu News – The Bengbu Special Products Collection and Transportation Office has been in operation for nearly two months. The collection and transportation area under its jurisdiction includes 21 counties in northern Anhui and 9 counties in central Anhui, totaling 30 counties. The collection and transportation period was originally limited to three months. However, due to the fact that three months may not be enough to complete the task, it is said that the collection quota for the 30 counties is set at 600,000 yuan. However, given the current situation of poverty among the people, it is doubtful whether the quota can be fully collected. Furthermore, due to the strict regulations of the office, each county's quota is too large, and the collection and transportation personnel must pay a deposit in advance and find a reliable shop as guarantor. Therefore, most people seeking collection and transportation jobs are taking a wait-and-see attitude, as there is a risk of compensation. It is reported that more than a month after the opening of the Special Products Collection and Transportation Office, only several thousand yuan in deposits have been collected. Commissioner Feng Yafo was quite anxious at first, but later decided to order all counties to start operations on February 1st, regardless of the circumstances. However, only ten or so counties have complied with the order. The collection and transportation personnel assigned to the remaining counties have been unable to travel as scheduled due to various procedures such as finding a guarantor and paying fees. Furthermore, Feng Yafo recently stated that many hotels, brothels, and opium dens in Bengbu City have a large amount of special products stored that have not been registered, and it is necessary to strictly crack down on them. Therefore, it was decided to establish an inspection station in Bengbu, appointing Li Rihui, a consultant of the office, as the director. After accepting the appointment, Li found a location in the Tongshang Apartment on Huachang Street and took office on the 6th, starting to work. The station has two departments: general affairs and inspection, and more than ten inspectors. Feng Yafo also issued a notice ordering people storing special products to report and register at the inspection station within three days from the 6th. However, given the strict attitude of the military and police authorities towards the prohibition of opium, whether people storing special products who register at the inspection station (paying an inspection fee of 30 cents per tael) and obtain an inspection certificate can have adequate protection from military and police inspections and arrests is a major question. (February 6th)

Yellow River Management in Shandong Province 104

Surveying and Repairing the Estuary, Adding and Repairing Stone Embankments, Preparing for Flood Control

Jinan Correspondence – The Yellow River has been a disaster for thousands of years, and Shandong, being located downstream, has suffered the most. Last autumn, the Ministry of Interior sent Wang Yingyu to Shandong to inspect the Yellow River with Pan Yifen, the Chief Engineer of the Shandong River Affairs Bureau, and Zhang Hanying, the President of the Jinan Branch of the Chinese Engineering Society. As a result, they believed that the most important thing for managing the Yellow River was to dredge the downstream estuary and add and repair stone embankments. Because the estuary is silted up, the discharge is not smooth, which leads to breaches. Where there are stone embankments, the water cannot erode them, so there have never been breaches. However, the project is huge, and due to financial constraints, it can only be done step by step. It is said that regarding dredging the estuary, the River Affairs Bureau plans to send personnel to conduct a preliminary survey and measurement after the spring warmth in order to design a plan. As for adding and repairing stone embankments, the province has already had two years of success. The method is to save other expenses, actively purchase stone materials, and it is estimated that in another two years, all the famous dangerous projects within the province can be completely converted from earth dikes to stone embankments. Then, even if there are major floods in summer and autumn, there will be no more breaches. However, ice floes are unpredictable. Ice floes are different from major floods in summer and autumn. Often, large ice floes dozens of feet across crash down from the upper reaches, and even giant trees dozens of feet in circumference will fall when hit. Ships are shattered when hit, and earth dikes and levees are even more easily destroyed. In addition, the weather is cold and the water is icy, so flood control personnel cannot enter the water and dare not approach. In the old rules of the Qing Dynasty, river workers were not punished for breaches caused by ice floes, which is the reason for this. This year, the weather is unusually cold. Around the Lunar New Year, the temperature in the province was often below 17 or 18 degrees Celsius, which has not been seen in decades. Therefore, the Yellow River has frozen thicker than in previous years. It is now after the Beginning of Spring, and large carts carrying thousands of pounds can still travel on the ice, so the thickness of the river ice can be imagined. Once the east wind thaws, the amount of river water and the force of the current will also be several times greater than in previous years. The River Affairs Bureau has already reinforced the secondary embankments and prepared water排 (bamboo rafts or barriers) to prepare for flood control. Although they are trying their best, they are not very confident. According to people at the River Affairs Bureau, the most terrible thing is that the weather is often cold and warm, and the ice may freeze and thaw at times, or the ice may thaw in the upper reaches and large ice floes crash down, while the lower reaches near the sea are still very cold and the ice has not yet thawed, which will block the ice and water from the upper reaches, causing it to crash in all directions, often leading to breaches. (February 7th)

Woodworking Business Owner Chopped by Unemployed Worker 105

Cheng Jin'gen, a resident of Village 56, Changqiao Township, Xinzhuang, Songjiang, is a carpenter. He runs a workshop at home and hires many workers to help with the work. Yesterday (the 7th), Yu Gengsheng, a worker who had quit, came from Qibao to ask Cheng for his remaining belongings. Cheng withheld them because of outstanding debts. Yu became angry and picked up an axe nearby, hacking at Cheng Jin'gen's back. The chop only broke his clothing. Yu then chopped at Cheng's chest but still did not cause injury. The worker then aimed a chop at Cheng's forehead. Cheng could not dodge in time and was struck, causing blood to flow all over the ground. Cheng was horrified and called another worker, Lu A'gou, for help. Lu helped to restrain the attacker, Yu Gengsheng, and hand him over to the police station to be transferred to the prosecutor's office for punishment.

Taicang Sixth District Murder Case Investigation 108

Xu Gui, a resident of Village 6, Township 15, Sixth District, Taicang, had a long-standing feud with his neighbor Chen Xinquan. They waited until the tide receded and then inserted Xu upside down into the mud. Xu's family searched all night after Xu was kidnapped but could not find him. The next morning, it was reported that Xu's body had floated up near Maocao Bridge. The case was immediately reported to the local public security bureau. Director Ma ordered the police to arrest the accomplices Xu Zuozhou and Xu Renqing. After preliminary interrogation, they confessed to kidnapping Xu Gui. Neighbors were awakened by the commotion. It was late at night and there was no time to call a doctor. By the next morning, all five members of the family had died one after another.

Implementation of the Abolish-Tael, Replace-with-Dollar Decision on March 1st 120

Weight: 7 mace 2 candareens; Fineness: .888

Officially Set Dollar Value: 7 mace 1 candareen 5 cash

The Mint to Simultaneously Begin Minting New Currency

Regarding the abolition of the tael and its replacement with the dollar, the Ministry of Finance convened a meeting of silver trade associations and expert committees on July 25th of last year to conduct research. However, due to unresolved issues such as the weight and fineness of the new currency, the matter was delayed. Recently, Minister Song met again with leaders of the silver and money industries. According to inquiries by a reporter from the New Voice Press, it has been decided to implement the change on March 1st. Details are as follows:

Weight and Fineness Determined: Minister of Finance Song Ziwen, in Shanghai, recently met again with leaders of the silver and money industries, believing that the abolition of the tael and its replacement with the dollar is a crucial step. Agreement was reached, and the weight and fineness of the new currency were determined, based on the principles of the Currency Regulations of the Third Year of the Republic. The weight will be 7 mace 2 candareens, equivalent to 23.9779048 grams, and the fineness will be .888.

Officially Set Dollar Value: Transactions in various industries are currently mostly calculated in silver taels. After the implementation of the abolish-tael, replace-with-dollar policy, it will be necessary to convert to silver dollars. If there is no specific method prescribed, difficulties will inevitably arise. The Ministry of Finance has now decided to set the official dollar value at 7 mace 1 candareen 5 cash per dollar. After implementation, all conversions between silver taels and silver dollars in various industries will be based on the officially set dollar value, thus avoiding conversion difficulties.

Implementation on the First of Next Month: As for the implementation date of the abolish-tael, replace-with-dollar policy, the Ministry of Finance has decided to implement it on March 1st of this year and will order all subordinate agencies to comply. However, as of last night, the local chamber of commerce and the trade associations of the silver and money industries had not yet received the ministerial order.

Free Minting of Silver Dollars: Since Director Guo improved the minting machinery at the Central Mint, the abolition of the tael and its replacement with the dollar will be implemented on March 1st. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance has decided to begin minting concurrently and to allow the free minting of silver dollars. That is, various industries can entrust the mint with the refining and minting of silver ingots. In the future, all silver dollars minted will feature the image of Sun Yat-sen and be new currency.

Money Industry Adopts Dollar Standard 121

Preliminary Measures to Be Implemented at the Beginning of the Month

Since the government officially promulgated the system of abolishing taels and using dollars, there have been repeated delays due to various inconveniences in commercial practices. Money shops, in order to adapt to the trend, have discussed the matter several times. Now, knowing that further delays are difficult, on the occasion of the traditional sacrificial rites to the industry's ancestors, leaders of the money industry gathered in the Yimiao Inner Garden. There, Runqing proposed that since the industry's exchange rate had already switched to the dollar standard, there was no need for daily fluctuations. A standard exchange rate should be set so that there would be a basis for silver-dollar exchanges. Furthermore, the appropriate steps to take after the abolition of the "foreign cash" should be determined. Discussion began immediately, and as a result, the following temporary measures were decided, to be implemented after being approved by a general assembly: 1. The standard cash price will be set at 7 mace 1 candareen 5 cash as a permanent dollar cash price. 2. Silver will be exchanged for dollars at a rate of 1 dollar and 40 cents per tael. 3. The exchange rate for subsidiary currency, which has previously been based on silver, will also be calculated using the dollar system from the date of implementation. 4. A dollar exchange market will be added, to be implemented from March 1st. The reporter notes that calculations based on items one and two show that when converting dollars to silver, 1,000 dollars in silver will only yield 1,398 dollars and 60 cents, which is 1 dollar and 40 cents less than the standard rate. When converting silver to dollars, 1,400 dollars can yield 1,001 taels of silver, which is 1 tael more than the standard rate per 1,000. For various industries, the small difference in commission is not a significant loss, while the financial sector will see no gain or loss. As for the conversion of subsidiary currency to the dollar system, let us provide an explanation. For example, if the current exchange rate is 6 mace for every 10 cents, then under the dollar system, it will be 84 cents of national currency. Increases or decreases in the exchange rate will be based on this standard. The same applies to copper coins. For example, if the exchange rate is 420 cash per thousand, then under the dollar system, it will be 300 cash (i.e., the standard for every 100 taels of silver or 100 dollars). This is the same as the exchange rates posted in the market, where every dollar is exchanged for 3,000 cash. Increases or decreases in the exchange rate will also be based on this standard. As for the issue of currency unification, it is feared that a decision cannot be made hastily. It will probably require some time after these measures have been implemented effectively and without unexpected disputes before it can be discussed.

Fire Destroys Trains at Zhabei Station 127

Three Passenger Cars Completely Destroyed, Others Damaged and Repairable; Losses Around 100,000; Cause of Fire Unknown

At 4:40 AM yesterday morning, a fire broke out in the Zhabei Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. Two empty passenger trains, each with more than ten empty passenger cars attached, were parked on Tracks 5 and 6 of the station. Unexpectedly, a first-class passenger car attached to the empty passenger train parked on Track 5 suddenly caught fire, and the flames quickly spread to the other passenger cars and the empty passenger train parked on Track 6. The wind was strong, and the fire burned until 6:00 AM, when it was finally extinguished. As a result, a first-class passenger car, a first- and second-class passenger car, and a third-class passenger car on Track 6 were completely destroyed, including their undercarriages. The estimated loss is around 100,000 yuan. The details are as follows:

Passenger Cars Parked: On the night of the incident, one empty passenger train, consisting of ten first-, second-, third-, and fourth-class passenger cars, was parked on Track 6 of Hangzhou Zhabei Station. This was the No. 38 express train from Shanghai North Station to Hangzhou, which usually departed at 4:10 PM and was parked overnight at Zhabei Station, ready to be used for the No. 37 express train from Hangzhou to Shanghai, which departed at 1:40 PM the next afternoon. Also, around midnight on the same night, another empty passenger train, consisting of twelve first-, second-, and third-class passenger cars, was parked on Track 5 of the station. This was the No. 32 special night express train from Nanjing to Hangzhou, which departed at 10:00 AM, but was delayed on the way that day, so it arrived at Zhabei Station at around 2:00 AM at night. After all the passengers disembarked, the driver shunted the empty passenger train and parked it on Track 5 overnight, ready to be used for the No. 33 special night express train to Shanghai, which departed at 6:35 AM the next morning.

Sudden Fire: Unfortunately, the disaster occurred on this train. After the driver of the No. 32 night express train from the capital shunted and parked the empty passenger train on Track 5 of the station, the first-class passenger car attached to the train suddenly caught fire at 4:40 AM the next morning. The flames spread rapidly, and the fire was fierce, with red light filling the sky. Because it was late at night, the station's traffic and mechanical staff, as well as the railway police, tried their best to put out the fire. However, the fire was too fierce and could not be extinguished easily. At that time, various fire brigades from Hangzhou heard the alarm and rushed to help put out the fire. It was not until 6:00 AM that the fire was completely extinguished.

Cause Unknown: The cause of the fire is still unknown. It is reported that the first-class passenger car that caught fire was equipped with electric lights, a meter, and hot water pipes. Therefore, it is speculated that the fire was caused by an electrical short circuit, the bursting of a hot water pipe, or someone leaving a cigarette butt. The exact cause of the fire is still unknown.

Destruction and Investigation: As a result of the fire, one first-class passenger car No. 203 (the passenger car that caught fire on the Shanghai-Nanjing line) and one first- and second-class passenger car No. 208 parked on Track 5, and one third-class passenger car No. 151 of the No. 38 empty passenger train parked on Track 6, were completely destroyed, including their car bodies and undercarriages. In addition, one other fourth-class passenger car and the roofs and windows of three adjacent passenger cars were also affected and damaged, but can still be repaired and used. The internal mechanical parts of the engine of the No. 32 train were also damaged. The estimated loss from the disaster is around 100,000 yuan.

Qu Wenliu Reports on the Suffering of Refugees in Northeast China 135

Qu Wenliu, the representative of the Shanghai United Association of Various Charitable Organizations for Relief of Northeastern Refugees, composed of nine charitable groups, who went north to investigate the situation, reported on the suffering of refugees in Northeast China at the Jiangxi Road Amei Broadcasting Station at 4:00 PM yesterday. He stated that this time, he was entrusted by the Shanghai Red Cross Society, the Chinese and Foreign Joint Relief Society, the Chinese Jisheng Society, the Lianyi Charity Association, the Huisheng Society, the Moral General Society, the Red Swastika Society, the Pushan Villa Xinwei Relief Society, and other nine charitable organizations to go north with Feng Yangshan, Wang Peiyuan, and others to organize relief for the Northeastern refugees. He went directly to Harbin once and to Qinhuangdao once, and investigated the situation in the war zones of Kailu, Xiawa, Suidong, Suizhong, and Lingyuan counties several times. Relief efforts are currently being actively carried out, and the amount of relief funds already released and being released exceeds 200,000 yuan. The trip to Harbin was made via the Beijing-Shenyang Railway directly to Liaoning, transferring to the South Manchuria Railway, passing through Changchun, and being subjected to surveillance and expulsion many times. The trip to Qinhuangdao involved working along the coast in icy and snowy conditions. As for Kailu, Xiawa, Suidong, Suizhong, and other places, trenches were dug and houses were torn down. The war situation can be described as being beyond human tolerance. Now that the war has been prolonged and the war zone has been expanded, the refugees between Shihe and Linyu mostly fled to Jinzhou, some to Beitianzhong, and some to Fangfu, Ningli, and Changli. Those who remained in Qinhuangdao were only in the dozens of villages nearby. From Kailu and Xiawa directly to Lengkou and Shihe, Japanese planes came to bomb from time to time. Remote villages and sparsely populated areas are far from the city, and no one goes to rescue them, and there is nowhere to escape. It can be said that there is no way to go to heaven and no door to enter the earth. The association's relief funds are limited and cannot provide full relief. It is hoped that all sectors will provide assistance.

Transforming the Great River Embankment into a Highway 136

The Executive Yuan Has Ordered the Two Ministries to Investigate and Handle

The China National Road Construction Association previously invited all sectors to visit the newly built embankments in Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Henan, and Shandong provinces by the National Government Flood Relief Committee. The association sent Wu Shan, a leading member, to participate in the inspection. After returning to Shanghai, he reported his findings to the executive committee, which decided to submit a request to the Executive Yuan to order the implementation of military engineering on the river embankments to convert them into highways to facilitate transportation. Afterwards, the association received a reply No. 21 from the Executive Yuan, stating that the submitted documents have been reviewed and that the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Military Administration have been ordered to investigate and handle the matter. This reply is for your information.

All Sectors Assist in Air Defense Equipment 137

The National Lawyers Association telegraphed to all lawyers' associations nationwide yesterday, stating that at the seventh standing committee meeting of the current session held by the association on February 1st, all members believed that in the Battle of Shanghai, the Japanese army relied on aircraft to carry out wanton bombing, turning the city into a heap of ruins, with blood and flesh scattered everywhere. The tragic scene was unbearable to recall. Now, the enemy is becoming more and more aggressive, and the disaster is becoming more and more urgent. If we do not rise up immediately and build air defense, then which of our splendid cities will not be a place for the Japanese army to drop bombs, and whose blood and flesh of our compatriots will not be targets for the Japanese army to drop bombs? Learning from the past and drawing lessons for the future, we are deeply shocked. Therefore, it was decided that the association will send a telegram to all member associations to jointly donate funds to purchase an aircraft, named "China Lawyers," to contribute to resisting the enemy. The donations will be collected and managed by the designated bank of the second executive committee of the current session from February 19th. This matter concerns a crucial plan to save the country, so we are sending this telegram to your esteemed association for your information and compliance. Please also reply. Furthermore, the staff of this association intends to make every effort to donate to promote the cause. We will deposit the funds as soon as the designated bank is determined and will telegraph again. Kowtowing from Liu Liumin, Jiang Yong, Yan Yinwu, Liu Zhe, and Dai Tianqiu, standing committee members of the Lawyers Association of the Republic of China.

Shanghai Lawyers Association: Yesterday, executive committee member Zhu Fuju submitted a proposal stating that he proposed donating one aircraft and one anti-aircraft gun to benefit air defense and promote the cause. Since the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident occurred, the Japanese army has been annexing our Northeast and ravaging our Shanghai, advancing step by step like a rapacious wolf and a long snake. To this day, Rehe is in danger, and North China is shocked. The enemy's disaster is deepening day by day, and the country is facing imminent doom. The most cruel weapon used by the Japanese army in its war of aggression is aircraft. Our soldiers who are resisting the enemy are bravely advancing, one falling and another following. It is not that the fighting is not strong, but that the weapons are insufficient. Among the weapons, those related to the air force are the most lacking, so we suffer significant sacrifices for no reason. People in the country are aware of this and are loudly calling for and promoting the air force, and many have already launched fund-raising efforts for aircraft. Every citizen is responsible for the rise and fall of the nation. The association has always been enthusiastic about patriotism and should immediately catch up and fulfill its duty as a citizen. However, while aircraft are important tools for air combat, anti-aircraft guns are also powerful weapons for air defense. If there had been one or two dozen anti-aircraft guns in the Battle of Shanghai, the Japanese aircraft would not have been able to wreak such havoc. Recently, the Northeastern volunteer army has also repeatedly called for the supply of air defense weapons. This shows that the importance of anti-aircraft guns is no less than that of aircraft. One focuses on increasing the efficiency of air combat, and the other focuses on resisting the enemy's power. The two complement each other and should not be neglected. Moreover, in terms of training personnel and various equipment, anti-aircraft guns are actually easier to implement than aircraft. With the enthusiasm of the members of this association and their ability, it should not be difficult to donate one aircraft and one anti-aircraft gun to achieve this goal. The righteousness will spread and surely attract more followers. Therefore, the method for raising funds is proposed as follows: 1. Appropriately allocate some public funds from the association. 2. Members should separately undertake fund-raising. 3. Deduct 5% of each member's public fees and remit them to the association once a month for a period of six months. The audit method will be determined separately. 4. Aim to raise 150,000 yuan. Is the above proposal appropriate? Please make a public decision.

Apostolic Delegate to China, Archbishop Celso Costantini, Returns Home Today 140

Catholics Prepare a Fond Farewell

Archbishop Celso Costantini, the Apostolic Delegate to China, has made meticulous plans and worked hard for the Catholic affairs in China since his arrival. Two years ago, Archbishop Costantini selected six Chinese priests and sent them to Rome, where they were personally consecrated by Pope Pius XI. After Archbishop Costantini and others returned to China, he assigned the six new bishops to reside in important dioceses. Recently, the country was divided into sixteen dioceses, and the church affairs have been thriving. In addition, he has also tried his best to assist in educational and charitable undertakings in various parts of China. Archbishop Costantini is particularly fond of China, so foreigners call him a "Sinicized Bishop." Archbishop Costantini followed the Pope's instructions and devoted himself to developing church affairs in our country. After residing in China for many years, he has become ill due to overwork and cannot be cured in a short period of time. Yesterday, he arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing and is scheduled to take a small ferry from the Customs Wharf to the Yangshupu Wharf at 5:00 PM today to board the Kenting ship to return to Italy for long-term rest. In this city, Lu Bohong has launched a campaign to invite Catholic organizations, the Shanghai Catholic Action Association, the Dongjiadu Fire Administration of the Shanghai South District, Zhengxiu, the First, Second, and Third Primary Schools, and a military band to go to the wharf to give a warm and grand send-off at that time.

Two Railways Ordered Zhongxing Coal 144

Total Quantity of 90,000 Tons at a Net Price of Ten Silver Dollars per Ton

At the end of last year, the Jinghu, Huhangyong, and Ningbo Railways, considering the large amount of coal used annually, and to save costs, intended to order national coal of excellent quality and reasonable price in batches. The matter was submitted to the Ministry of Railways, which entrusted the Purchasing Committee to order 90,000 tons from Zhongxing Company. The price per ton, including all taxes and fees, was ten national dollars, a particularly favorable price, unprecedented. Delivery would be at Pukou. The Purchasing Committee has already signed the contract. The quality, composition, and inspection procedures have also been specified in detail. Therefore, recently, the two railways have prepared a large number of trains, ships, and workers to unload and transfer the coal at Pukou to various stations. The first batch of goods will be cleared soon. The bureau has also selected capable staff to go there to supervise the weighing and other matters to avoid losses.

Yu Yan Discusses the Reorganization of Railway Operations 145

| Two Points Contributing to Future Directions |

Yu Yan, Director of the Operations Department of the Ministry of Railways, discussed the reorganization of railway operations over the past six months and the future direction as follows: 1. Responsible Transportation of Goods: The effectiveness of responsible transportation has been proven by facts. According to the Jinpu Railway, since the full implementation of responsible transportation, the revenue for November of the 21st year was 2,161,886.66 yuan, while the revenue for the same month of the 20th year was 1,619,299.43 yuan, an increase of 542,587.23 yuan. This increase is by no means solely due to the increase in freight rates. Moreover, the Jinpu Railway's revenue in recent years has mainly come from passenger transport. Comparing the same months of the two years shows that the main reason for the increase is that freight transport exceeded passenger transport, which is very clear. Secondly, comparing December of last year with the same month of the previous year, the movement of troops and the transportation of military pay and equipment were continuous, and military transport was extremely busy, with almost all vehicles being used for military transport. However, the increase in revenue still reached 225,030.86 yuan. Furthermore, in the first ten days of January this year, there was also a significant increase of 249,506.61 yuan compared to the same period of the previous year. The above increases are all based on facts and can be made public. Secondly, after the January 28th Incident, the Jinghu and Huhangyong Railways suffered heavy losses, and their capacity was insufficient. However, the revenue from freight transport alone on the Jinghu Railway in November of the 21st year still increased by more than 60,000 yuan compared to the same month of the previous year. Of this, responsible freight charges only accounted for slightly more than 20,000 yuan, and the rest was the actual increase in freight revenue. Due to the Yuguan Incident, the situation changed in December of the 21st year, and freight transport was inevitably affected. However, it still increased by more than 5,900 yuan compared to the same month of the 20th year. The fact that this railway, despite being dilapidated and suffering significant losses of locomotives and vehicles, was still able to achieve this result is a good sign for the future of responsible transportation. (To be continued)

Municipal Bank to Add a Trust Department 147

Merger of Savings and Remittance Bureau Not Yet Resolved 148

Ministry of Communications Has No Concrete Merger Plan; Postal and Telegraph Associations Advocate Maintaining the Postal System

According to postal worker sources, postal services have been affected since the separation of the Savings and Remittance Bureau. In May of last year, the Postal and Telegraph Associations firmly proposed a plan to consolidate the foundation of the postal service, first advocating the abolition and merger of the Savings and Remittance Bureau as the right way to save the postal service. The government, in view of the past failures of separation, first accepted the principle of merger and established a Postal Economic System Research Committee to discuss the implementation of the merger. Since its establishment, progress has been slightly delayed due to political changes in the middle. Since Minister Zhu took over, the Postal Research Committee has handed over the preparation of the report to a special committee, which is generally quite detailed. Unexpectedly, Minister Zhu sent a letter to the Postal Research Committee, seemingly agreeing in principle, but the implementation plan for how to merge was vague and without concrete expression, resulting in the Postal Research Committee's work being delayed. Recently, the Ministry of Communications appointed Tang Baoshu as the new director and made large-scale changes to the directors and other office staff within the bureau. This kind of treatment not only violates government orders and the solution to the resumption of work, but also clearly shows that they have no intention of implementing the merger and maintaining the postal system. It is reported that the Postal and Telegraph Associations are submitting opinions to the Postal Research Committee and presenting them to the Ministry of Communications for attention. As for the rumors that the matter has been resolved, they are not true.

Automatic Telephones in the Chinese Area to Be Installed Next Month 149

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has begun installing automatic telephones and is expected to complete the installation by the end of next month. There are more than 2,000 households in Nanshi, about 400 in Zhabei, and about 100 in Pudong. The number of people installing them has been increasing recently. Regarding the issue of dismissing switchboard operators after the automatic telephones are in operation, the person in charge of the bureau said yesterday that they plan to dismiss those with poorer performance or assign them to work in the long-distance telephone department. As for the main switchboard of the long-distance telephone, it will be moved to Zhabei after the automatic telephones are completed.

Case of Postal Workers Arrested in Beiping 151

Trade Union Asks Mrs. Sun for Assistance; Huang Naishu Says He Has a Solution

According to the New Sound News Agency, after thirteen executive committee members of the Beiping Postal Workers' Union were arrested by the Beiping military police authorities on the 2nd of last month, the National Postal Workers' Union sent representatives to Beiping to investigate the truth. Yesterday, the Beiping Postal Workers' Union sent a telegram to Mrs. Sun Yat-sen (Soong Ching-ling), requesting assistance. However, according to Postal Director Huang Naishu, the matter has a solution. The information obtained is recorded below:

Telegram to Mrs. Sun 152

The Beiping Postal Workers' Union sent a telegram to Mrs. Sun Yat-sen (Soong Ching-ling): Mrs. Premier, regarding the matter of appealing for assistance, the Beiping Post Office and Postmaster Bali Di, (an Italian), colluded with the military police on February 2nd to arrest all thirteen executive committee members of the Beiping Postal Workers' Anti-Japanese Association. Immediately thereafter, a bureau notice was issued, dismissing the thirteen people on the grounds of disobeying orders, neglecting bureau affairs, falsely accusing superiors, and violating the postal code. The thirteen people are loyal comrades of our association and have been very active in working hard to resist Japan. Even if resisting Japan is a violation of the postal code, it still falls within the scope of the postal service and does not bear criminal responsibility. Why should they be arrested and detained? Moreover, they have been detained for more than 24 hours and have not been handed over to the court, which is a trampling of human rights. This is the first point. The Beiping military police authorities do not distinguish between right and wrong, acting as accomplices, surrounding the post office, closing down the trade union, arbitrarily interfering in post office affairs, and unreasonably arresting and detaining civil servants, which is also illegal. This is the second point. The thirteen people are members of the Anti-Japanese Committee. The military police authorities and the postal authorities must get rid of them at all costs. Is the authorities hindering resistance to Japan? This is the third point. We respectfully present an outline and ask you to quickly telegraph the Beiping authorities to immediately restore the work of the thirteen people. The situation is urgent, and we cannot help but wait for orders in trepidation. Mrs. Soong Ching-ling has already telegraphed the Beiping authorities yesterday to release them.

Huang Naishu's Remarks 153

Yesterday, the reporter of the New Sound News Agency visited Director Huang Naishu of the Postal Bureau again to ask about the truth of the matter. According to him, the reason for the arrest of the Beiping Postal Workers' Union members was actually because of the serious situation in North China, the precautions were extremely tight, and those who were slightly active, like those making trouble, would be arrested to prevent accidents. This is one of the measures taken by the Beiping military police authorities to maintain local peace. The postal authorities had nothing to do with it. However, after the National Postal Workers' Union sent personnel to investigate, a telegram was received today saying that there was already a considerable solution.

Peculiar Death of a Rickshaw Puller 157

At around 2:00 pm yesterday, a rickshaw puller, about 40 years old, wearing black cotton-padded jacket and pants, a Russian hat, and straw sandals, pulling a rickshaw with city license number 6823, stopped his vehicle near Sanpailou in this city. He parked the vehicle on the side of the road and sat on the footboard with his eyes closed, appearing to be resting quietly. Unexpectedly, he never woke up and died. Passersby noticed and immediately reported the situation to the Second Precinct of the First District. The precinct chief, considering the peculiar death and the matter involving a possible homicide, immediately ordered Hua Wenrong, the local headman, to report to the Shanghai Local Court for an autopsy.

County Finance Bureau to Be Abolished 158

The Shanghai County Government has received an instruction from the Jiangsu Provincial Government stating that, due to the financial difficulties of the province and counties, austerity measures should be implemented to save money and increase administrative efficiency. The various bureaus of the county should be appropriately abolished and merged. Only those bureaus that can comply with this order will be allowed to operate. It is known that, in addition to the Public Security Bureau, which had already changed from a bureau to a section, the remaining bureaus are the Finance, Construction, and Education Bureaus. It is now learned that the Finance Bureau has been ordered to be abolished and merged, and its functions will be handled by a section established by the County Government. The Education Bureau, due to its annual education expenditure exceeding 120,000 yuan, will not be abolished. The Construction Bureau, due to the need for planned construction after the county seat moves, will also not be abolished for the time being. County Finance Director Wang Huazhao has ordered the sections to expedite the completion of the closure of the bureau by March 1st, so that it can be handed over to the County Government at that time.

Minutes of the General Meeting of the Department Store Guild 163

The Municipal Department Store Trade Association held a general meeting of members the day before yesterday, attended by representatives from Huigong, Yifeng, Dalu, Miaoji, Hongxing, and others. Zheng Hairuo was elected chairman. After formal procedures, the following resolutions were passed: 1) Promote domestic goods: The association will issue notices to all businesses in the city to (a) actively promote domestic goods, (b) encourage customers to use domestic goods, and (c) department store merchants must use domestic goods. 2) Rectify the external credit of members: In the future, any member of the same trade who arbitrarily declares liquidation with the intention of obtaining illegal benefits will be immediately expelled from the association and publicly announced. 3) Department store market project: Zhang Wei, Zheng Hairuo, Wang Jiying, Zhang Lixing, Chen Huiqing, Jin Binglan, Lu Yongzhang, Ke Yuyuan, and Zhang Shaozhai were elected as committee members to be responsible for the project. 4) Send letters to all manufacturing factories stating that the retail prices of products sold in their distribution outlets or companies must not be lower than the wholesale prices, so as to avoid damage to the business of the association. 5) In the future, any price increases or decreases of goods from factories should be justified and formally notified to the association first. After obtaining the association's consent, the trade will be notified. 6) Notify members that if manufacturers arbitrarily reduce prices without the association's consent, causing business damage to members of the association, they may request assistance from the association to protect their interests. 7) Recruit members: Wang Weiying was appointed as the commander of the recruitment team, and Zhang Wei, Li Shanfu, Ling Shaoxuan, Chen Huiqing, Zhang Lixing, Hua Minghui, Zhang Shaozhai, Jin Binglan, Ke Yuyuan, Wang Fangting, Xia Zhihong, Cheng Guichu, and Lu Yongzhang were appointed as division leaders to actively carry out the recruitment.

Italian Rayon Imports Valued at 7 Million Yuan 167

A Total of 1,750 Pieces Were Imported, and Chinese Businessmen Plan to Invest in Establishing a Rayon Factory

At a time when China's silk exports are sluggish, rayon imports are again crowded. The silk fabrics exported by China's silk mills all use rayon. Although the customs has increased import duties, imports decreased last year. However, due to increased demand in China, rayon imports have surged again in recent days. The details are recorded below.

Large Batch Arrives 168

Rayon manufactured and shipped from Italy is considered the best. The best-selling products on the market are those from the Chatillon and Cisa factories. After the Ministry of Finance increased the import tax on rayon last year, it was temporarily hindered. However, recently, the products of Chinese silk mills cannot appeal to buyers without mixing rayon, so they are purchased at high prices. The Italian mail ship Ganqi arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday, carrying a large batch of 1,750 pieces of rayon, with a total value of 7 million yuan including the price of goods and customs duties. This is the first large amount of rayon imported this year.

Stored in Customs Warehouse 169

The price of each piece of rayon, weighing about 200 pounds, is about 130 taels of Shanghai silver. In the past, the import tax was calculated at 75% of the value, about 10 taels of silver per piece. Last year, the Ministry of Finance revised the tariff regulations and listed it as a luxury item, increasing the import tax to 99 taels, 1 mace and 8 fen per piece. The second revision of the tariff rate changed the goods to 124 taels, 8 mace and 3 fen per piece. Converted from 141 customs gold to silver, each piece must be over 160 taels of standard silver. The large amount of rayon brought this time requires a tax of over 3.8 million taels just for customs duties. The importing foreign firms do not have such a huge amount of money to pay, so yesterday they stored the goods in the customs warehouse, and will pay taxes on each piece when they are sold and unloaded.

Handling Firms 170

The foreign firms in Shanghai that handle the import of rayon are Tianyou, Huajia, Kaili, Anli, Meizuishi, Anmao, and others. The largest businesses are Tianyou and Anli, which purchase and ship over a thousand or hundreds of pieces each time. The sales in Shanghai are to silk mills in Zhejiang Province, and some are shipped to the Yangtze River and the north and south oceans. Rayon is also shipped from Japan, but the quality is not as good as the Italian goods, and the price is lower. After the January 28th Incident last year, the import of Japanese rayon was not as high as before. Recently, it has been smuggled in secretly from Dalian.

Factory in Shanghai 171

A reporter met someone in the industry yesterday who said that Chinese businessmen are jointly investing with foreign businessmen to establish a rayon factory in Shanghai, manufacturing it locally for use by various silk factories. According to estimates, the cost of manufacturing each piece of rayon in Shanghai is only over 10 taels, plus the factory tax, which is only a tenth of the current import price. This matter is already being planned.

Prize Exhibition Held at the New World Company, Dance Girls Participating in Tea Dance Also Receive Prizes

Major Gambling Den Cracked Down in Zhenru 173

Public Security Bureau Dispatched Police at Midnight, Detaining a Total of Eighty-Nine Gamblers

Yang Miaogen, a local thug in Zhenru Town, has no legitimate occupation. Recently, he has been using the Lunar New Year as an excuse to set up a gambling den on North Street in the town, taking a cut for profit. According to reports, the Municipal Public Security Bureau secretly dispatched detectives the night before to arrest them, detaining a total of eighty-nine people. The details are recorded below.

Yang the Thug Taking a Cut 174

Yang Miaogen was originally a vagrant. Since opening the gambling den at the beginning of this year, he has been luring good people in the town to gamble, and Yang has been reaping the profits. As a result, his daily life has also been different from the past, and his methods are generous. Those who do not know think he is a wealthy man. Zhenru is far from Shanghai, and gamblers in Shanghai heard about this place and flocked to it. As a result, Yang's daily income has also doubled.

Cracked Down at Midnight 175

Because the gambling den still had to avoid people's eyes during the day, it was even more popular at midnight. After receiving reports, the Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatched a large number of detectives to Zhenru on the night before to cooperate with the Fourth District Third Precinct to carry out the arrest. When they arrived, they heard a noisy commotion in the house, and they were in high spirits. Fearing that the gamblers would escape, the detectives surrounded the house and then knocked on the door. Unexpectedly, the gamblers inside heard someone knocking on the door and knew something was wrong, so the order was disrupted and they fled in all directions. How could they know that they had been surrounded and were stopped one by one? A total of eighty-nine people were detained. That night, because they could not transport them all to Shanghai, they were detained overnight at the Fourth District Third Precinct. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the General Bureau along with the gambling equipment for investigation. Yang Miaogen, the leader of the gambling, was also among them.

Further News on the Tragic Case of Arresting Gamblers in Wusong Paotaiwan 176

Hu Changxiu Killed in Police Shooting Case

Regarding the case of Gu Damao's family at No. 10, Gujiazhai, behind the old site of the China Public School in Wusong Paotaiwan, where police officer Hu Changxiu was shot and killed while arresting gamblers the day before yesterday, it is learned that the information contained in the report is slightly different. Yesterday, a reporter conducted an investigation and described the details as follows. It turned out that around 1:00 PM on the day before yesterday (the 7th), the Seventh District Police Station received a report that someone had set up a gambling den in that area. District Chief Li dispatched Inspector Yang Xihui, Patrol Captain Wang Xindong, Dong Jingyun, Jiang Zhixiu, and police officers Hu Changxiu, Li Zongchen, Peng Xuede, etc. to arrest them. When they arrived at the scene, they first secured the front and back doors of the house. At that time, there were about forty gamblers in the house, all trying to rush out the door. Some of the fierce ones, seeing that there were not many police officers, punched and injured Patrol Captain Dong Jingyun in the head. Seeing that the situation was not good, Patrol Captain Dong immediately drew his gun and fired two shots into the ground. At that time, the gamblers were still rushing outwards, pushing police officer Hu Changxiu to the ground. Unexpectedly, a bullet fired from Patrol Captain Dong's gun hit police officer Hu Changxiu in the neck. At that time, the order was slightly chaotic, and about twenty gamblers took the opportunity to escape. As a result, Gu Damao, Gu Guilin, Pu Fusheng, Jin Yunqing, Fei Amao, Fei Xiaodi, Pu Alin, Zhang Ada, Pan Baotang, Zhang Genhe, Zhang Ali, Liu Shenggen, Pan Jinsheng, Pan Aji, Zhang Qingqing, Zhang Xilin, Shen Asheng, Hu Gensheng, Jin Lansheng, and other nineteen people were detained and taken to the district for interrogation. The injured police officer Hu Changxiu was immediately sent to the Shanghai Baolong Hospital for treatment, but died on the way. The body was transported back to Wusong and temporarily placed in the Chu Laoda Temple. Yesterday, a report was filed with the local court, and Prosecutor Zhang was dispatched to Song to examine the body, confirming that he had died from gunshot wounds. Patrol Captain Dong, who caused the accident, was interrogated by District Chief Li yesterday. He confessed that when he fired a gun to warn, police officer Hu was pushed to the ground by the gamblers, resulting in accidental injury and death. After interrogation and verification, the gamblers were notified by long-distance telephone to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, which dispatched a red car to transfer Patrol Captain Dong and the gamblers to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for handling. According to District Chief Li, Patrol Captain Dong has been working in Song for many years, and has always been very diligent and has not made any mistakes. This accidental death of Hu Changxiu is a truly unfortunate incident. He is now trying to comfort the family of the deceased and find ways to mitigate the punishment for Patrol Captain Dong. As for the gamblers, there was no firing of guns.

Apprentice's Theft Leads to a Luxurious Dream of More Than a Month 177

Departed from Shanghai with a Huge Sum of 1,500 Yuan

500 Yuan Stolen on the Train, Dared Not Speak Out

After Arriving in Jiaxing, Gambling Friends and Lewd Women Continued Day and Night

Money Exhausted, Returned to Shanghai in a Sorry State, From Now on, Tasting the Flavor of Iron Bars

Dai Yuanbing, an apprentice from Anhui at the Zhengda Silk Factory at No. 168, Tianjin Road, is only twenty-one years old. He is usually diligent in his service and is quite favored by Manager Jiang Guoxiang. On December 20th of last year, Jiang ordered Dai to take a check for 500 yuan from the Bank of China and a check for 304 yuan from the China Trust Bank to the Tonghe Bank on Ningbo Road for deposit. Unexpectedly, Dai suddenly had a greedy idea and did not comply, but instead took the Bank of China check to the Bank of China and cashed it for 500 yuan. Because the China Trust Bank was far away, he tore up the check. Then, he stole a seal from the Zhengda Silk Factory and forged a check for 1,000 yuan, and went to the Notification Bank to get 1,000 yuan. In total, he cashed a total of 1,500 yuan from the Bank of China. So he abandoned his job and fled with the money. The silk factory did not know where he had gone and could not find him, so they had to report to the authorities to issue a warrant for his arrest. In fact, Dai took the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to Zhejiang Province. Unexpectedly, when the train arrived at Jiaxing Station, 500 yuan of the huge sum he was carrying was stolen by thieves. He had only 1,000 yuan left in his pocket, and he dared not speak out, but only sighed. He had no intention of moving forward, so he stopped at the Huaan Hotel at the North Gate of Jiahe. The waiter of the hotel, Jv Sheng, saw that Dai was sparsely dressed but had a lot of money in hand, and mistakenly thought he was a wealthy man who came to Jiaxing to play. He introduced local dandies and prostitutes, and they spent time together day and night. After more than a month, the 1,000 yuan he brought was lost 800 in gambling and 200 in whoring. The hotel owner ordered him to leave. The old gambling friends and lewd friends all avoided him. Dai began to feel sorry for himself, but he was lonely and helpless in a foreign land. There was no point in staying, so he returned to Shanghai the day before and hid in the Huping Hotel on North Fujian Road. After thinking it over again, he felt that his uncle Jiang Dizhai had always treated him well and might be able to help him. Therefore, he telephoned Dizhai and told him his reckless history, saying that he only had suicide as a way out, begging him to remember their past friendship and come to see him for the last time. Dizhai told his brother Jiang Guoxiang and reported to the Laozha Public Security Bureau, which dispatched detectives Wang Jiaju and Li Shugui to the hotel to arrest Dai. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Local Court, where Judge Feng Shide interrogated him. Zhang Shizhu, the lawyer of the Public Security Bureau, stated the case, saying that the defendant had committed the crimes of embezzlement in violation of Articles 357 and forgery in violation of Article 224 of the Criminal Law, and should be punished according to law. Dai Yuanbing fully admitted to the charges. Judge Feng immediately sentenced each crime to one year in prison, to be served concurrently for a term of one year and six months. This is truly reaping what he sowed.

Coal Merchant Pan Gengsheng's House Robbed Yesterday 178

Losses Exceeded 6,000 Yuan

Pan Gengsheng, from Wuxi, is 59 years old. He used to be a lime barge operator. Recently, he has been a broker for the Kaiping Coal Mine's Shanghai depot, and rents a front room on the second floor of the Shenlongtai Foreign Iron Shop at No. 114, Xiamen Road, as a residence. Pan usually lives frugally, so he has saved a little money over the years. Unexpectedly, he was coveted by bandits. At around 8:30 AM yesterday morning, Pan had just finished washing up and was about to send the collected coal money of about 5,000 yuan to the Wufeng Money Exchange for storage, when he suddenly heard a knock on the door. Pan asked who it was, and the person outside the door replied, "Open the door, Boss Pan." Pan thought it was a coal customer urging for coal, so he opened the door. Unexpectedly, the three people who came were strangers. After entering the room, they took out handguns and ordered Pan Gengsheng to open the silver box in the room, or they would kill him. Pan had no choice but to take out the key and open the silver box, allowing them to search it. However, the bandits saw that the upper drawer in the box was locked and could not get started, so they turned around and ordered Pan to open it again. Pan firmly refused. At that time, one of the bandits saw that Pan was holding a bunch of keys tightly in his right hand, so he stepped forward to grab it. The victim resisted with all his might. The bandit, in a hurry, bit Pan's right thumb and the back of his hand. Pan was in extreme pain and released his hand. The bandits were able to open the upper drawer and plunder everything. Seeing that they had achieved their goal, the bandits tried to escape, but were afraid that Pan would take the opportunity to call for help, so they pushed Pan into the middle floor when they left, and locked the door from the outside and fled. The victim saw that the thieves had gone far away, so he tried his best to call for help. Later, a friend of Shenlongtai downstairs heard about it and released Pan, who rushed to report to the police and requested to pursue the thieves. It is said that one of the three thieves was wearing a blue cloth gown, about forty years old, and two were wearing brown coats, both in their twenties, with local accents. The victim's losses included a pair of gold bracelets, ten gold rings, and more than 5,000 yuan in cash, totaling about 6,000 yuan.

Record of Continued Hearing of the Running Dog Association's Lawsuit Against Martin, etc. 180

Special Use of Dog Race Betting Proceeds

Allegedly for Payment of Stamp Tax to the Central Government

The Running Dog Association, due to the closure of the Ming Garden Dog Racing Track, sued Martin, the current acting Chief of the Public Works Bureau's Police (who was the acting Chief at the time), and former Chairman of the Board MacNaughton, seeking damages of 2.5 million taels. The hearing continued the day before yesterday afternoon before Sir Grain, the British Receiver, with the plaintiff's witness, Mr. Bowyer, a shareholder of the Thomson & Co. and former secretary and accountant of the Running Dog Club, giving his testimony. The hearing continued yesterday morning at 10 a.m., with Mr. Bowyer being cross-examined by Mr. Huber Bowe, the defendant's chief lawyer. However, the questions all concerned the Running Dog Club, and Mr. Bowyer often appeared hesitant and embarrassed in his answers. (Note: The Running Dog Club is another organization formed by the people of the Running Dog Association, engaged in running the dog races. The Running Dog Association, the plaintiff in this case, is a limited company that owns the dog racing track and leases it to the Club. Therefore, the grounds for the lawsuit are mainly based on preventing people from entering the park.) Several points particularly caught the attention of the entire court during yesterday morning's questioning. One was that in the income and expenditure report of the Club for the year ending October 1930, it was noted that the Club set aside 11% of the dog race betting proceeds, with 1% for a special purpose. When Mr. Huber Bowe asked what that special purpose was, the plaintiff's lawyer immediately approached the defendant's lawyer for a brief whispered conversation. Then, the defendant's lawyer consulted with the two defendants. Finally, Mr. Bowyer was asked to answer, and he stated that it was reserved for paying stamp tax to the Central Government. Subsequently, Mr. Huber Bowe intended to continue questioning the details of paying this tax, but Mr. Bowyer was unwilling to answer and the matter was dropped. Regarding the program offered by Ming Garden Lu and the automobile company for 30 cents, which included a free one-yuan admission ticket, the defendant's lawyer pointed out that it was an official program. However, Mr. Bowyer was unable to clearly explain whether it was an official program or an unofficial one. Another time, Mr. Huber Bowe questioned the advertisement fee of 44,800 yuan, asking what the purpose of this advertisement was. He asked if the Club was truly willing to spend 44,800 yuan annually just to invite people to the park to watch dogs, and wasn't the purpose of extensively advertising in newspapers to entice people to come and bet on the dog races? At that moment, the audience burst into laughter. Mr. Bowyer's response was remarkably calm, stating that he simply wanted people to know that there were dog races taking place in the park. After Mr. Bowyer finished testifying, Mr. Adams, the secretary of the China Business Company, was called to testify. However, because the documents needed to prove Mr. Adams' testimony were not yet prepared, he was asked to leave and scheduled to testify again in the afternoon.

Kidnapping Bandit and Informant in Trouble 181

Commotion Erupts in Detention Center

Bandit Accuses Informant of Being an Accomplice

Fang Jinhong, a Cantonese man and the Import Department Director of Sincere Company, was previously kidnapped by bandits. Fang resisted during the abduction, leading to his murder by the bandits. Later, based on information from an informant, the police of the Mixed Court arrested ten bandits, including Zhang Qishan, and handed them over to the First Special District Court for trial. The trial concluded on the morning of the 7th, with sentences pronounced. The news was reported yesterday. It is now known that the informant's name is Cao Houfu (also known as Zhao Xinggui), 37 years old, from Tongzhou, living on Longjiang Road. He usually works as a vendor at a stall at the intersection of Changping Road and Gordon Road in West Shanghai. Since reporting Zhang Qishan and others for the kidnapping case, Zhang and others implicated him in the case during the trial, even vaguely suggesting that he was the ringleader. However, the authorities feared that this was a malicious accusation and did not immediately arrest him, continuing a secret investigation. On the 6th of this month, Cao was arrested by the Yulin Road police for gambling at Lan Road. The next morning, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court, where he was fined six yuan. According to the customary procedure of the police, criminal offenders who have been tried must be taken to the detention center on the side of the Special Court's main gate before being transported back to the police station in batches by prison van, in accordance with the court's instructions. Therefore, after Cao's fine was determined, he was taken by the police from the Eighth Court to the detention center to wait for the prison van. It happened to be the day that the bandits, including Zhang Qishan, who murdered Fang Jinhong, were sentenced. Moments after Cao entered the detention center, Zhang and the other nine bandits were sentenced by the Second Criminal Court and escorted back to the detention center. At this point, enemies met, and their eyes were particularly sharp. Zhang Qishan, upon entering the detention center, suddenly saw Cao already there. He immediately scolded him sharply, accusing him of leaking information. The other nine bandits also joined in the attack, and Cao became the target of everyone's anger. The patrol officers in the detention center initially did not know the reason for the bandits' difficulty with Cao. While stopping the commotion, they asked what was going on. Zhang and others unanimously claimed that Cao was their accomplice and the ringleader. The patrol officer reported this to his superiors, who ordered Cao to be taken to the Yulin Road police station for investigation. Because Zhang Qishan and his gang of bandits were arrested by the police of the Mixed Court, and Cao was accused of being an accomplice, and the case involved kidnapping, extortion, and murder of the hostage, both the truth and falsehood should be thoroughly investigated. For the sake of convenience, Cao was still sent to the Mixed Court police station for investigation by experienced personnel. Yesterday morning, Detective Wang Youshan of the police station escorted Cao to the First Special Court, where Judge Qian Wenqiong interrogated him. First, Wang Yaotang, the police station's lawyer, explained the situation and requested that Cao be temporarily detained for investigation. However, according to Cao's statement, his fellow villager, Hu Guangshan, recently came to Shanghai from their hometown, saying that a girl in their family was kidnapped by Zhang Qishan's gang. Because I knew Zhang, he asked me about Zhang's whereabouts. On December 29th, while I was running my stall at the intersection of Changping Road and Gordon Road, I saw Zhang and four or five others entering a teahouse there to drink tea. I remembered Hu's words and paid attention to them. Later, I reported it to my friend Chen Laosi. Chen is a detective, and later Chen and Chinese and foreign detectives arrested Zhang and others. I have a family to support and would never be a bandit. I am being falsely accused. Judge Qian then ordered Cao Houfu to be detained and investigated, with a new hearing date to be scheduled.

Ministry of Railways Reduces Freight Rates for Ceramics from Pottery and Porcelain 182

The Ministry of Railways recently stated that pottery produced in Boshan, Shandong Province, is essential for the daily use of ordinary people, such as jars, basins, pots, bowls, cups, bottles, plates, and casseroles. These are the crudest ceramics produced by local handicrafts and are vastly different from porcelain from Jiangxi. The original freight rates were the same as for other porcelain, classified as fifth class, which was inconvenient. Now, for the sake of local industry, these crude ceramics will be reclassified as sixth class. Finer materials, such as teapots, teacups, wine cups, plates, dishes, pots, bottles, and bowls, will still be charged at the fifth class rate to show differentiation. The "Ceramics and Kiln Goods" item in the Ministry's Freight Transportation Classification Table will be modified, divided into three classes: special products from Jiangxi, Hebei, Henan, Zhejiang, Guangdong, Shandong, and other provinces will be classified as fourth class; superior products will be classified as fifth class; and ordinary products will be classified as sixth class. Orders have been issued to all routes to collect freight according to the class to ensure uniformity.

Da Zhen Company Adds New Yong Ji Steamer 183

Shanghai Da Zhen Shipping Company has owned the Yong Ping and Yong An steamers that operate on the Shanghai-Sea routes. Since its establishment, it has strived for perfection in its facilities. It has built warehouses in Shanghai and Dapu, which are very large and provide responsible protection for passengers and goods, avoiding exposure and leakage. It has always been praised by customers, and its business is developing daily. Due to the continuous flow of goods from the Longhai Railway, the company's original two steamers are insufficient for transportation. A new Yong Ji fast steamer has been added to the fleet. The steamer has a deadweight of 3,000 tons and a shallow draft. It officially began operating on February 6th.

Dredging of Shanghai South Pier No. 9 Completed 184

Dredging of No. 8 Will Also Begin

Shanghai South Pier No. 9 has been completed with funds advanced by the Lian An Shipping Bureau. However, due to the high silt accumulation on the shore, it is difficult for ships to dock, so the pier has not been equipped. The Municipal Public Works Bureau previously consulted with the Whangpoo Conservancy Bureau to send a machine to dredge the area. It is reported that the work has been completed, with a total of 6,000 cubic yards of silt removed. Pier No. 8, which is adjacent to Pier No. 9, is also experiencing increasing silt accumulation, making it impossible for ships to dock even at high tide. It is reported that the Public Works Bureau has obtained approval from the Municipal Government to dredge it as well. Construction will begin soon, and there should be no difficulties for ships to dock side by side in the future.

Reader Advice 188

How to Achieve Local Autonomy? 189

丨Continuing yesterday's reply to Mr. Lü Jingming's letter丨

㈡ You said: [China was originally a large agricultural society, so local autonomy should start in the countryside], which is also self-contradictory. You said earlier that [true local autonomy in a region must be successful after the economy and culture have been developed to a considerable stage]. Then, we must ask: Where does the economy and culture of the countryside come from? Obviously: Where do the machines and plows needed in rural areas come from? Where do the primary school teachers needed in rural areas come from? Where do the books for establishing libraries in rural areas come from? Doesn't all of this require the city to supply it? Doesn't it require the economy and culture of the city to reach a certain stage of development? Since the economy and culture of the city must first develop to a certain stage before rural autonomy can be discussed, then what does your statement that [local autonomy should start in the countryside] really mean? Now that the city has achieved a considerable development of its economy and culture, but you don't let it start with autonomy, isn't this treating the people in the city like [idiots]? Why are you so partial to the countryside and treat the city so poorly? The most illogical argument of the general public in China is the saying that [China is founded on agriculture]. Those who say this think that only China has been founded on agriculture from ancient times to the present, and that it is an unchanging and unique social phenomenon. In fact, this is an illogical argument for those who do not understand the history of social development and do not read Western history. At a certain stage of historical development, a country must go through the form of development of a rural economy. The only difference is that some are long and some are short. If you understand this point, then you will not use the words "founded on agriculture" as China's patent. The economic systems of almost all European countries in the Middle Ages were founded on agriculture. France was still an agricultural country during the era of the Great Revolution. The United States also had a rural economy dominating in its early stages. Russia was still a huge, simple agricultural country in the early 19th century. How can the claim that [China is founded on agriculture] or, as you said, [China was originally a large agricultural society] be used as the basis for starting local autonomy in the countryside? However, the advocacy of this kind of argument that [China is founded on agriculture] by a group of Chinese gentry and the ignorant teachers in most educational circles is not blind and unintentional, but rather has their own interests as a backdrop. In general, representatives of landlords and feudal remnants want to use this theory丨China is founded on agriculture!丨as a smokescreen to cover their conservative or regressive tendencies. To be honest: only the city leads the form of social development in the countryside; there is no form of social development in the countryside leading the city (of course, to some extent, changes in the countryside can also affect the city, but this is not the main and leading role). So, to talk about local autonomy, it can only start with the city. This is one point. Local autonomy is not an isolated social phenomenon, but rather the entirety of the entire social political organization and economic system. If you talk about local autonomy apart from the entire social change, then you are really only seeing the trees and not the forest. This is the second point. As we have mentioned earlier, true local autonomy is not a peaceful favor given by law or command, but rather the result of mass social movements. Local autonomy that is not obtained from actual actions is merely an officially permitted local official's autonomy, and it is just another form of autocracy. This is the third point. Local autonomy is unconditionally universal. It cannot be used as an excuse to withhold it due to some level of economic and cultural development. This is the fourth point. As for what you call [experts in people's education], they cannot be regarded as a prerequisite for local autonomy, let alone the main body of local autonomy. They are merely a kind of machine, a kind of tool, a kind of technical talent of local autonomy. That is to say, their research is not [a glimmer of dawn for the future of rural governance], but rather the urgent need for autonomy felt by the largest majority of the masses in the countryside. Everyone uniting and going to the streets to do actual work is the true glimmer of dawn for local autonomy. This is the fifth point. What do you think? ㈢ We have not seen the full text of Mr. Liang Shuming's criticism of rural autonomy, but just based on the points you mentioned, we can see a glimpse. Mr. Liang's words originally had a metaphysical tinge everywhere, and we really don't understand some of his remarks. ㈠ [If we increase the wealth of the countryside in the same way as running schools, then I'm afraid it will be very trivial]. Then, what method should be used to increase the wealth of the countryside? And what kind of method is the so-called [method of running schools]? This is a kind of indiscriminate statement. ㈡ [Industry must be developed before culture can be improved]. Who will develop this industry? For whom will this industry be developed? And what kind of culture is the so-called culture? Mr. Liang did not add detailed boundaries, so it is still a kind of indiscriminate statement. ㈢ [Using the method of running education to carry out rural improvement movements will inevitably lead to the road of losing both talent and money]. This is again creating mystery! What kind of [method of running education] is Mr. Liang talking about? Why, when the method of running education is applied to rural improvement movements, does it have to [lose both talent and money]? Indeed, this kind of method of running education itself will collapse. Not only will it lose both talent and money when applied to rural improvement movements, but it is also afraid that it will not be able to avoid this kind of malpractice even when applied to education itself. In reality, the words "losing both talent and money" are simply incomprehensible! Mr. Liang should still go and talk about his [㈠ Western life is the intuitive use of reason: ㈡ Chinese life is the rational use of intuition: ㈢ Indian life is the rational use of immediate experience]. It's good to talk about those mysterious idealist philosophies. If he wants to talk about our local autonomy, we really don't need his high-level theories! As for what you call [what else can we do? What other brilliant methods are there?], after reading our explanations above, perhaps you will no longer have such doubts, right? What do you think?

Guidelines for Submitting Articles to the National Goods Weekly 190

㈠ This publication is seeking the following types of manuscripts: (1) Research on national goods | factories and domestically produced raw materials: (2) Discussions on improving the production and sales of national goods. (3) Records of lectures and talks on the national goods sector: (4) Introductions to new national goods industries: (5) Interviews with national goods industries and their leaders: (6) News on national goods: (7) Other interesting and valuable texts, photos, and drawings related to national goods.

㈠ There are no restrictions on the style of manuscripts, but the main emphasis is on being concise, insightful, and lively. The length of each article should be around 500 characters. Articles with special value should not exceed 1,000 characters at most.

㈠ Manuscripts must be written clearly and use modern punctuation.

㈠ Authors are free to choose whether to sign their names when manuscripts are published, but they must indicate their real names and detailed addresses at the end of the manuscript and affix a seal.

㈠ The editor reserves the right to make revisions to manuscripts. Authors who do not wish to have their manuscripts revised must state this in advance.

㈠ Manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not, unless they are pre-marked and accompanied by a stamped envelope.

㈠ A remuneration will be paid for manuscripts that are published.

㈠ Please send manuscripts directly to the editorial department of the National Goods Weekly at the Shen Bao.
